target="_blank">Unsplash</a></figcaption></figure><h1 id="8dcb" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Executive Summary</h1><ul class=""><li id="3caf" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">According to an analysis report published by InterLab in December 2022, a South Korean journalist received a message requesting a conversation via the Wechat messenger, and the requestor instructed the journalist to install a malicious APK file disguised as a messenger called “Fizzle.apk” — InterLab named the malicious APK &quot;RambleOn&quot;</li><li id="1472" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">We found similar features and codes to the mobile version of the ROKRAT malware that the <a class="af oq" href="https://attack.mitre.org/groups/G0067/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Scarcruft</a> group has been using since 2017.</li><li id="24c1" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">In tracking the Scarcruft group, researchers within S2W&#x27;s Talon have identified additional samples that perform similar functions to those disclosed in this release, with significant upgrades from previous releases.</li><li id="0360" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Scarcruft is strongly believed to conduct initial penetration by contacting individuals directly via messengers, such as in this case, to trick them into installing a malicious APK disguised as legitimate.</li><li id="1e7b" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">S2W Talon named &quot;<strong class="my gv">Cumulus</strong>&quot; in reference to past samples similar to the type of malware disclosed by InterLab, and named the plugin used by Cumulus as &quot;<strong class="my gv">Clugin</strong>&quot;.</li><li id="3076" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">There are three types of Cumulus, depending on whether or not the Clugin is downloaded and the type of messaging service used.</li><li id="dfdb" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">We observed that the Scarcruft group updated the malware&#x27;s functionality or installed China-specific applications on test devices to target users with Chinese language and Chinese-manufactured mobile devices.</li></ul><h1 id="3403" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Introduction</h1><p id="7348" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">The Scarcruft Group (aka APT37), a North Korean APT group, is believed to have been active since 2016 and continues to carry out attacks against institutions and political organizations around the world until 2023. In April 2017, the Cisco Talos team disclosed the Scarcruft group&#x27;s proprietary tool, ROKRAT, a malware that has been continuously modified and used by the group to this day. Initially, only the Windows version of ROKRAT was used, but the Android version of the malware was later identified.</p><p id="c587" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">According to a report published by the Financial Security Institute, the Scarcruft group conducted an attack in mid-2017 that distributed malicious APKs to specific devices through a watering hole attack. At the end of 2017, the group also carried out an attack campaign targeting North Korean human rights organization officials and journalists from North Korean media outlets to induce the installation of malicious APKs through KakaoTalk, the most popular messenger in South Korea. In addition, malicious APKs were also distributed by contacting targets through Facebook and uploading APKs to the Google PlayStore. The malicious apps were all identified as mobile versions of ROKRAT.</p><ul class=""><li id="b5ff" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Reference: <a class="af oq" href="https://www.fsec.or.kr/bbs/detail?menuNo=244&amp;bbsNo=6139" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">[FSI] Threat Intelligence Report - Campaign DOKKAEBI</a></li></ul><p id="1aa0" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">According to an <a class="af oq" href="https://interlab.or.kr/archives/2567" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">analysis report published by InterLab in December 2022</a>, during a conversation with a South Korean journalist via Wechat messenger, the Scarcruft group convinced him to install a malicious APK file disguised as a messenger called &quot;Fizzle.apk&quot;, saying that he could not send sensitive files via Wechat messenger. InterLab named the malicious APK &quot;RambleOn&quot;, but analysis of the malicious APK revealed similarities to the Scarcruft group&#x27;s ROKRAT mobile version. Unlike in the past, the APK has the ability to receive data from the attacker via a messaging service called Pushy.</p><p id="a3af" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In following the Scarcruft group&#x27;s trail, Talon, S2W&#x27;s threat research and intelligence center, identified additional samples that perform similar functions to the published samples. They have similar functionality to the malicious APKs released in 2017, but unlike in the past, the ability to use messaging services has been added. We also found that these APKs have been continuously updated to date. S2W Talon named the malicious APKs &quot;<strong class="my gv">Cumulus</strong>&quot; and the plugin modules used by Cumulus &quot;<strong class="my gv">Clugin</strong>&quot;.</p><p id="da68" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In this report, we further categorize the identified Cumulus by type and describe the attacker&#x27;s TTPs and strategy based on our detailed analysis.</p><h1 id="dbb4" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Overview of Cumulus Types</h1><p id="3e15" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Cumulus (aka. RambleOn) has been used by the Scarcruft APT group since at least 2019 to target Android devices. The group has been using a mobile version of the ROKRAT malware since at least 2017, and S2W Talon separately classifies Cumulus as a type of existing ROKRAT mobile malware with messaging capabilities such as FCM or Pushy added. Cumulus is usually distributed disguised as a legitimate mobile application, such as a CoinMiner, image viewer, or messenger. Although we could not secure more samples, we have also seen them distributed under the package names &quot;com.personal.info&quot;, &quot;com.sec.mishat&quot;, and &quot;com.data.person&quot;. Based on the types of applications Cumulus disguises, we suspect that it is distributed directly to individuals via messengers, such as this RambleOn type.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qc"><picture><source type="image/webp"/><source data-testid="og" srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/1*6DSAm1qYa2VmhjKiaHipBg.png 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/1*6DSAm1qYa2VmhjKiaHipBg.png (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2.5) and (max-width: 700px) 80vw, (min-resolution: 2dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px"/><img alt="" class="bh md ol c" width="700" height="688" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Table 1. Types of Cumulus</figcaption></figure><p id="70c9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">After obtaining additional Cumulus disguised as legitimate applications and analyzing them, we were able to categorize them into three types, as shown below. Types B and C download a separate plugin and perform their main actions in the plugin, which is why we named the plugin downloaded by Cumulus as <strong class="my gv">Clugin</strong>.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qd"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/format:webp/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 720w, type="image/webp"/><source data-testid="og" srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 720w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:750/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 750w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:786/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 786w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:828/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 828w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:1100/1*zfGppuhXGBkLZvniT7oXAA.png 1100w, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2.5) and (max-width: 700px) 80vw, (min-resolution: 2dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px"/><img alt="" class="bh md ol c" width="700" height="155" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Table 2. Type Classification</figcaption></figure><ul class=""><li id="f6bb" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Clugin</strong>: Plugin that Cumulus downloads from the cloud and is responsible for information leakage.</li><li id="d19a" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">Command</strong>: Configuration file that a Clugin or Cumulus downloads from the cloud to execute commands.</li><li id="0848" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk"><strong class="my gv">CallRecorder</strong>: An additional Dex file that the Clugin or Cumulus downloads from the cloud to perform call recording functions.</li></ul><p id="ff6d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Type A</strong> downloads and loads the <strong class="my gv">Command file</strong>, which contains the configuration information necessary to perform the malicious behavior, and <strong class="my gv">CallRecorder</strong> from the cloud. It then uploads the infected device information and internal files to the cloud. It receives a separate message from the attacker via FCM.</p><p id="4faf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Type B</strong> downloads the <strong class="my gv">Clugin</strong> from the cloud. Clugin takes over the functions of Cumlus, downloads <strong class="my gv">Command file</strong> and <strong class="my gv">CallRecorder</strong>, steals and uploads information to the cloud. Compared to Type A, by introducing Clugin, Type B organizes modularization by function and secured stable persistence and malware update function. Same as Type A, Type B receives a separate message through <strong class="my gv">FCM</strong>.</p><p id="0297" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">TEST</strong> seems to be used by the attacker for testing before the attack and uploads the infected device information and internal files to the cloud without downloading any additional files. Cumulus, which is used in real-world attacks, uses abbreviations to upload each exfiltration data to the cloud, but in the case of TEST, the full word is used for ease of identification during the test.</p><p id="7974" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Type C</strong> has most of the same features as Type B, but uploads the Device Token to the cloud instead of the Firebase Database and receives messages from the attacker via <strong class="my gv">Pushy</strong>.</p><p id="c874" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">FCM is a service that specializes in message delivery within <a class="af oq" rel="noopener" href="/s2wblog/unveil-the-evolution-of-kimsuky-targeting-android-devices-with-newly-discovered-mobile-malware-280dae5a650f">Firebase and was also used in the mobile malware used by the Kimsuky group that we disclosed last year</a>. The difference is that the Device Token is sent to the cloud or a legitimate Firebase database, rather than to an attacker&#x27;s C&amp;C server. The most recent version of the Pushy service is a separate third-party service that provides similar functionality to FCM.</p><h1 id="97b3" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">TimeLine</h1><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qe"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/0*sFnhb1z5G5nADEfj 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/format:webp/0*sFnhb1z5G5nADEfj 720w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:750/0*sFnhb1z5G5nADEfj 750w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:786/0*sFnhb1z5G5nADEfj 786w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:828/0*sFnhb1z5G5nADEfj 828w, du">Figure 1. Full Timeline for Cumulus</figcaption></figure><p id="df27" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Clugin appears to have been uploaded to Yandex Cloud and distributed since at least September 2021. Although we do not have an exact date for the creation of Yandex Cloud, we believe that Clugin distribution began around that time. The pCloud account was subsequently created in October 2021, but the data exfiltration we identified was from March 2022. Given that Type B was distributed in March 2022, we believe that the attacker began distributing Clugin via pCloud in a similar way. The attacker appears to have initially distributed Clugin through Yandex Cloud, and then, starting in March, configured it to communicate with pCloud on initial infection and only communicate with Yandex Cloud when passing a separate command. TEST is believed to be a test version to introduce this. The Scarcruft group appears to have set the OAuth key for pCloud communication differently for each distributed APK but kept the OAuth key for the Yandex cloud relatively unchanged.</p><h2 id="1e51" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">1. Behavior flow for Type A</h2><p id="6f2b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">After infection, <strong class="my gv">Type A</strong> registers a method to JobScheduler to periodically execute the main malicious behavior. It then downloads a Command file from the Yandex cloud and steals information as specified in the Command file. It additionally downloads and loads a CallRecorder, which performs call recording and saves it to a file.</p><p id="ab18" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The collected infected device information and internal files are uploaded to Yandex, which also transmits the device token for FCM communication, allowing the attacker to obtain the Device Token of the infected device from the Yandex cloud. The attacker can use the obtained Device Token to send a message to the infected device via FCM, and Cumulus, which receives the message, checks whether the method that performs the malicious behavior is registered in the JobScheduler and registers it if it is not.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qe"><picture><source srcSet="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:640/format:webp/0*VLm1xwoQt4PovvPD 640w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:720/format:webp/0*VLm1xwoQt4PovvPD 720w, du">Figure 2. Execution flow of Type A</figcaption></figure><h2 id="b44b" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">2. Behavior flow for Type B</h2><p id="1eaf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Cumulus in <strong class="my gv">Type B</strong> downloads the Clugin from the cloud, then the Clugin downloads CallRecorder, and steals the infected device information and internal files. In addition, Type B receives messages via FCM, adding update functions such as changing cloud storage and changing OAuth Token.</p><p id="83d1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">When executed, Type B first sends the Device Token to the Firebase Database. With the sent token, the attacker passes the OAuth Token and the cloud REST API through FCM, which is presumably used to download the Clugin from the cloud. At the time of analysis, we were unable to obtain actual data from FCM, but based on the internal code of Type B, we believe that it is downloaded from Yandex Cloud.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of du">Figure 3. Execution flow of Type B</figcaption></figure><h2 id="bbbe" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">3. Behavior flow for TEST</h2><p id="8f19" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">In the case of<strong class="my gv"> TEST</strong>, when the APK is executed, it steals information such as infected device information, SMS, contacts, internal files, and recordings and uploads them to the pCloud. Although TEST includes Yandex Cloud&#x27;s OAuth Token, it actually uses only pCloud&#x27;s OAuth Token initialized within the pCloud SDK class and does not use the Yandex Token. In addition, there is no function to send the device&#x27;s Device Token separately, so we assume that Type A is for testing purposes only. The string &quot;test-pi-d9b7e&quot; is used in the code to initialize Firebase functionality, and the functionality is incomplete compared to other types, suggesting that the attacker used this type for testing.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qu"><picture><source du">Figure 4. Execution flow of TEST</figcaption></figure><h2 id="8257" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">4. Behavior flow for Type C</h2><p id="1c05" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Type C</strong> sends messages to Cumulus via a third-party messaging service called Pushy rather than FCM. Type C has both hardcoded pCloud and Yandex&#x27;s OAuth Token values, and an attacker can update the type of cloud service and OAuth Token via Pushy.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz Execution flow of Type C</figcaption></figure><h1 id="17ec" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Detailed Analysis</h1><p id="50e7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">We conducted a detailed analysis of a messenger impersonation APK called &quot;Fizzle&quot; (named RambleOn by Interlab) and Clugin version 6.0, which is classified as <strong class="my gv">Type C of Cumulus types</strong>. Below is the entire execution process of a Type C Cumulus.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz alt="" class="bh md ol c" width="700" height="704" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Figure 6. The communication scenario of Cumulus</figcaption></figure><h2 id="d0a8" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Stage 1: Cumulus (Fizzle.apk)</h2><p id="c0e7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">1. Status in SharedPreferences</strong></p><p id="175f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Cumulus manages the status with SharedPreferences and references it to perform its malicious behavior. The <em class="nx">UUID</em> or <em class="nx">TID</em> in the status is used as an ID to identify the infected device. Initially, it uses the <em class="nx">UUID</em>, but if it subsequently receives a message from the attacker via Pushy, it changes the ID to the <em class="nx">TID</em> contained in the message instead of the <em class="nx">UUID</em>. Then, store the Device Token for receiving messages from Pushy in <em class="nx">PUSHYT</em> and set <em class="nx">CLOUD</em> to P to communicate with pCloud. The OAuth Token required for cloud communication is specified in <em class="nx">PRIMARY_ACCESSTOKEN</em>. Also, set the Clugin version to <em class="nx">VERSION</em> to request the Plugin{<em class="nx">VERSION</em>} file to the cloud, and set the download success to 1 or 0 in <em class="nx">PLUGINDEXDOWN</em>{<em class="nx">VERSION</em>}. <em class="nx">CLOUD</em> is only supported for P (pCloud) and Y (Yandex), and is set to P on the first run.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qw"><picture><source alt="" class="bh md ol c" width="700" height="318" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Table 3. Values in status</figcaption></figure><p id="29a2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">2. Download Clugin from Cloud</strong></p><p id="058e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Cumulus references the status to download the Clugin in Dex form from the cloud service. Since the cloud identifies infected devices by their UUID or TID values, it is possible to install a different Clugin for each device. After downloading, it calls the LogState method of the com.personal.info.plugin class.</p><ul class=""><li id="7268" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt Downloads Clugin and invoke</figcaption></figure><h2 id="7c77" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">Stage 2: Clugin (DEX)</h2><p id="7765" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Cumulus downloads and executes Clugin in the form of plugin from the cloud. In this process, we were able to collect samples of different versions of Clugin, between 1.0 and 6.0. After analyzing each version of the Clugin, the table below summarizes the versions and features that we found to have noticeable changes.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz Feature comparison table of Clugin by version</figcaption></figure><p id="c8c1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">1. Download Command file from Cloud</strong></p><p id="8f9b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The Clugin reads the Command file from the cloud and performs information theft according to the values set in each field. For each field, the data is specified in the format {Type} : {Key} : {Value}, and the Key and Value are parsed and registered in SharedPreferences. The C(Command) file can be deleted from the cloud after downloading.</p><ul class=""><li id="06ce" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw Keys in Command file</figcaption></figure><p id="3d9e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The CMD in the Command file determines whether malicious behavior is performed.</p><ul class=""><li id="e17a" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">CMD == 0: Do not perform malicious behavior</li><li id="3fd9" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">CMD &gt; 0: Run the service and send the information after stealing it</li><li id="7e42" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">CMD &gt; 10: Download and load CallRecorder</li></ul><p id="8637" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">2. Interact with Cumulus to execute malicious services</strong></p><p id="bbe6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The Clugin checks whether the AR and SDPATH values are set in the Command file and executes the malicious behavior by interacting with Cumulus. If CMD is greater than 0 in the Command file, the Clugin checks to see if a specific service in Cumulus is currently running, and if not, executes the service through an Intent. The service in Cumulus directly calls specific methods in the Clugin to perform the actual audio recording or file collection behavior. In the figure below, Clugin checks whether a service named &quot;com.sec.mishat.{ServiceName}&quot; is running, which is the package name of Cumulus. The reason for this implementation is that the commands are modularized using Clugin, so the version of Clugin can be updated at any time, taking advantage of the fact that Clugin does not depend on Cumulus. The malicious behavior executed in this way is as follows.</p><ul class=""><li id="e8e8" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Update Clugin from the cloud</li><li id="e5d8" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Audio Record using CallRecorder</li><li id="1562" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Collect files from external storage</li></ul><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" Collect &amp; Exfiltration</strong></p><p id="f011" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Finally, Clugin collects information from the infected device and sends it to the cloud. List of collected data and upload path</figcaption></figure><p id="1674" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">For the stolen items stored in the D path on the cloud, encryption is performed before exfiltration, which involves downloading an epk file containing the encryption key from the cloud. The file data is then AES decrypted and Base64 decoded with hardcoded values in Clugin to extract the RSA public key. Each collected file is then encrypted by randomly generating an AES secret key, and the secret key is encrypted with the extracted RSA public key. Finally, the encrypted file data is stored along with the encrypted AES secret key, length of encrypted AES secret key, Custom Path, and length of Custom Path. If the RSA public key does not exist, the generated AES secret key is stored in plain.</p><ul class=""><li id="934d" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt qwertyuiop456789</li></ul><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qe"><picture><source role="presentation"/></picture></div></div><figcaption class="om ff on ny nz oo op bf b bg z du">Figure 16. Execution flow when receiving a message from Pushy</figcaption></figure><h1 id="271b" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Interesting discoveries</h1><p id="7f41" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">We have been monitoring the group’s attack campaign for a few months and have been able to obtain data from victims compromised by Cumulus and Clugin, as well as test data from attackers leaked by OPSec failures. We were able to see malicious app deployment tests and the context of malicious app distribution via messengers.</p><h2 id="1873" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">1. Targeting Chinese Phones</h2><p id="ebe7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">The Scarcruft group has traditionally implemented its messaging capabilities through Firebase, but in the latest version, it uses a third-party service called Pushy. This is believed to be in case the targets use mobile devices made in China, such as Huawei. In fact, Pushy reviews indicate that many people have switched from Firebase to Pushy to ensure a stable implementation in China.</p><h2 id="fa67" class="qf os gu bf ot qg qh dy ox qi qj ea pb nh qk ql qm nl qn qo qp np qq qr qs qt bk">2. Installed Packages in Test Environment</h2><p id="cb64" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">We found that the attacker was testing the malicious APK. From the test logs, we could see the information of the attacker&#x27;s test device, and from the installed application information, we could see that VPN and translation applications were installed.</p><p id="5f55" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Astrill VPN is used as a VPN application to bypass internet blocking in China, and SpeedCN is an application that increases the speed of Internet access in China. The presence of a translation application that can translate Chinese among the installed applications suggests that the attacker is preparing to target Chinese-speaking users.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="oh oi fj oj bh ok"><div class="ny nz qw"><picture><source Installed packages on the test device</figcaption></figure><h1 id="bbb3" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Attribution</h1><p id="2085" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt gn bk">Our analysis of the Cumulus and Clugin samples reveals a strong similarity in code and functionality to malicious APKs distributed by the Scarcruft group in the past through watering hole attacks. The malware used was a mobile version of ROKRAT, which suggests that the Scarcruft group continued to update it and use it to this day.</p><ul class=""><li id="d653" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">Reference: <a class="af oq" href="https://www.fsec.or.kr/bbs/detail?menuNo=244&amp;bbsNo=6139" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">[FSI] Threat Intelligence Report - Campaign DOKKAEBI</a></li></ul><p id="c936" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The malicious APK used by Scarcruft in 2017 drops an additional malicious APK with the package name &quot;com.android.systemservice&quot;, and code similarities between the APK and Clugin 6.0 were found. The same routine for downloading Command files from the cloud and registering settings via SharedPreferences is present in both malware. We also found the same values for the keys registered by the 2017 sample and those in the Command downloaded by the 2023 sample.</p><figure class="ob oc od oe of og ny nz paragraph-image"><div pj pk pl pm pn po bk">Conclusion</h1><ul class=""><li id="c998" class="mw mx gu my b mz pp nb nc nd pq nf ng nh pr nj nk nl ps nn no np pt nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">We found that the Scarcruft group has continued to improve the mobile version of the ROKRAT malware they have been utilizing since 2017 and is still actively using it today.</li><li id="983b" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">The mobile version of the ROKRAT malware can be classified as Cumulus, which receives messages from attackers via messaging services such as FCM or Pushy, and exfiltrates data to cloud services such as pCloud and Yandex.</li><li id="d4ef" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">As disclosed by Interlab, the group is conducting attack campaigns targeting individuals and using conversations to convince them to install malicious apps disguised as legitimate apps, such as image viewers, messenger programs, etc.</li><li id="92c9" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">A multi-channel strategy that utilizes cloud services such as Yandex and pCloud, as well as legitimate services such as Firebase and Pushy for command and control.</li></ul><h1 id="ab29" class="or os gu bf ot ou ov ow ox oy oz pa pb pc pd pe pf pg ph pi pj pk pl pm pn po bk">IoCs</h1><blockquote class="nu nv nw"><p id="cd66" class="mw mx nx my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Full IoC list can be found our <a class="af oq" href="https://github.com/S2W-Talon/Threat-Intelligence-Report/blob/main/230323_Scarcruft%20Bolsters%20Arsenal%20for%20targeting%20individual%20Android%20devices/IoCs.md" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">github</a></p></blockquote><ul class=""><li id="d284" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">5dde5f5fcc1ebfd932e1ef0bfcc7b272</li><li id="379f" class="mw mx gu my b mz px nb nc nd py nf ng nh pz nj nk nl qa nn no np qb nr ns nt pu pv pw bk">957ebfbd0b23a164529d7510ca89ddae</li><li
